ISLAMIC REPUBLIC OF MAURITANIA
EDUCATION SECTOR RESTRUCTURIN(o RPOJECT
Proiect Manaaement and Responsibilities for Project Coordination
1.        Background.  The current Project Coordination Unit (PCU) created
under the Second Education Project and located in the Ministry of Economy
and Finance, with a very small staff (i.e., director, administrator and
support staff) has performed well during the second project implementation;
it would be retained and strengthened. This decision is in line with the
multi-sectoral approach of the project which involves the Ministries of
National Education, Economy and Finance, Fisheries and the Ministry of
Labor.
2.        Obiectives.  To amplify the institution-building effect of the
project, its various components would be implemented by the concerned
Directorates of the Ministries mentioned above. However, in view of the
size and the short period of implementation (five years) of the project,
the main objective of this component is to ensure adequate institutional
and administrative arrangement to successfully implement the project, while
reinforcing and developing the managerial capacity of variouis Ministries
concerned. Intermediate objectives include: (i) supporting the
Government's institutional building policy; (ii) placing project management
at a sufficiently high and independent level in the Ministry of Economy and
Finance to provide inter-departmental and inter-ministerial coordination;
(iii) making individual managerial units responsible for the implementation
of the project components directly related to them; and (iv) serve as
liaison between IDA, the project agencies and the Government.
3.        Approach/strategy.  To this end, the implementation
responsibility for this project would be assumed by the Project
Coordination Unit (PCU) with the responsibility for individual project
components and sub-components decentralized to the concerned directorates
and department. The PCU would remain attached to the Ministry of Economy
and Finance, and would be headed by a full-time national Project Director,
assisted by the current management team reinforced by (i) an architect (for
the first three years of the project) to assist in the implementation of a
hardware components and procurement, and (ii) an accountant.
4.        Functions.  With responsibility for overall supervision and
guidance of project implementation, the project director would oversee the
coordination of all project activities, including liaison with the
different units of other ministries and government services concerned with
the project, and would serve as the direct contact point between the
Government and IDA. More specifically, the PCU would:
(a) assist each Directorate in the preparation of annual work programs and
budgets for the implementation of each project component;



- 145 -
ANNEX 3-16
Page 2 of 6
(b) prepare all necessary documentation for the annual review of the
Action Plan made jointly by the Government and IDA, and act as the
secretariat of the Government's review committees
(c) coordinate all aspects of project implementation with the relevant
Government entities;
(d) ensure that those responsible for each component carry out their
functions effectively;
(e) supervise the preparation of bidding documents and handle jointly with
institutions concerned the procurement of civil works, good and
specialist services in line with IDA's guidelines;
(f) plan and carry out all procurement functions, and ensure that goods
and services procured under the project are delivered to their
destinations and utilized adequately;
(g) arrange for the recruitment of personnel and specialists required by
the project;
(h) monitor and administer the specialist service contracts for both
qualitative and quantitative conformity with contract obligations
(short-term as well as long-term) and training/fellowship programs
(local and abroad);
(i) ensure adequate Government counterpart funding is budgeted and monitor
the satisfactory flow of funds for the project components (from
counterpart, IDA, AfDB, communities and private sector sources);
(j) prepare and maintain all project accounts, following accepted
accounting formats and procedures;
(k) prepare all necessary documents for withdrawal of funds from the local
project accounts (Special Account for IDA financing and separate
accounts for the counterpart funds) and for submission of withdrawal
application to IDA;
(1) arrange for annual and semi-annual audits of all project accounts by
auditors selected following IDA guidelines and ensure that such audit
reports are forwarded to IDA within six months after the end of each
fiscal year;
(m) keep records, including financial records of the project, and submit
to IDA semi-annually progress reports on project implementation and a
completion report no later than six months after completion of the
project; and
(n) arrange for the preparation of future projects.



- 146 -
ANNEX 3-16
Page 3 of 6
5.        Means.  In order to carry out its responsibilities, the PCU will
be staffed with the following personnel, all adequately qualified and
experienced:
Permanent Staff           Status         Functions
(a)  a full-time Director      local          project management
(b)  an Administrator          local          financial/contracts management
(c)  an Architect              foreign        implementation/procurement
(d)  an Accountant             local          accounting
(e)  an Administrative
Secretary                 local
(f)  Support Staff             local          two typists, two chauffeurs,
four orderlies
Additional support staff would be provided on a needs basis by current
civil servants. In addition, the project would finance the following
specialist services (short-term consultants) to assist the PCU in specific
areas:
Short-term specialist          Status         Duration
(a)  educationalist                 foreign           3 mlm
(b)  procurement specialist         foreign           6 m/m
(c)  financial analyst/legal        foreign           5 m/m
(d)  auditors                       foreign          5 m/m
(e)  short-term specialists
for future project
preparation                    foreign          30 m/m
Cf)  mid-term review                foreign        0.3 m/m
Finally, the project makes provision for minor office building repairs and
the necessary office equipment, transport and operating costs for the PCU
during project implementation.

ANNEX 3-21
Page I of 3
ISLAMIC REPUBLIC OF MAURITANIA
EDUCATION SECTOR RESTRUCTURING PROJECT
Procurement Procedures
Part A.   Procurement of Goods and Works
1.        Except as provided for in Part C hereof, goods (furniture,
non-pedagogical equipment and pedogogical materials) shall be procured
under contracts awarded in accordance with procedures consistent with those
set forth in Sections I and II of the "Guidelines for Procurement Under
IBRD Loans and IDA Credits' published by the Bank in May 1986 (the
guidelines).
Part B.  Preference for Domestic Manufacturers
2.        In the procurement of goods in accordance with the procedures
described in Part A. 1 hereof, good manufactured locally may be granted a
margin of preference of 15Z in accordance with, and subject to, the
provisions of paragraphs 2.55 and 2.56 of the guidelines and paragraphs 1
through 4 of Appendix 2 thereto. Procurement under local procedures does
not qualify for preference.
Part C.   Other Procurement Procedures
3.        All civil works contracts and goods contracts estimated to cost
the equivalent of between US$15.000 and US$150,000 equivalent per contract,
which are not likely to attract overseas foreign firms, would be procured
under contracts awarded on the basis of competitive bidding, advertised
locally (LCB), in accordance with procedures satisfactory to the
Association, provided that: (i) the aggregate amount of such procurement
shall not exceed the equivalent of US$5.9 million equivalent: (ii) all bids
shall be opened in public: (iii) criteria for evaluatina bids shall be set
out clearly and communicated to all bidders: (iv) no preference margin
shall be granted to domestic manufacturers or suppliers: and (v) foreign
companies shall not be required to be incorporated in Mauritania in order
to participate in the bidding.
4.        Items (office supplies, spare parts, gasoline) that cannot be
grouped into bid packages of at least USS15.000 equivalent provided the
aggregate amount of such procurement shall not exceed US$4 million
equivalent, would be procured through international and local shopping on
the basis of quotations obtained from at least three foreign or local
suppliers in accordance with procedures acceptable to the Association.



- 163 -
ANNEX 3-21
Page 2 of 3
Part D.   Review by the Bank of Procurement Decision
1.   Prior Review
5.        For all contracts or bid packages of at least US$150,000
equivalent, each of the following stages in the procurement process would
be subject to IDA's prior review and commented upon by IDA staff before
they are implemented and finalized:
-    Advertisement
-    Prequalification (if called for)
-    Bidding documents and addenda
-    Bid evaluation and proposal for award of contract
-    Contract documents
-    Subsequent major modifications of the contract
2.   Initial Review
6.        For all contracts valued at up to US$150,000 equivalent, an
initial review, followed by a post review or a random review depending on
the size of the contract, by IDA staff would be required for standard
documents which are common to a number of procurement operations, for
example:
-    the general format of advertisements and their circulation;
-    the prequalification questionnaire and method of evaluation;
-    standard registers of prequalified contractors; and
-    standard bidding documents, including instruction to bidders,
general conditions of contract and, in some instances, technical
specifications.
3.   Post Review
7.        For all contracts or bid packages estimated at between US$15,000
and US$150,000 equivalent, two copies of the final contracts, together with
the bidding documents, bid evaluation and award decision, would be
furnished to IDA for post review before the first application for
withdrawal of credit fund against these contracts.
Random Review
8.        The provisions of the preceding subparagraphs of Part D, (1), (2)
and (3) shall not apply to contracts valued at under US$15,000 equivalent
on account of which the Bank has authorized withdrawals from the Credit
Account on the basis of statements of expenditure. Such contracts shall be
retained at the Project Coordination Unit for random review by IDA
supervision missions and for regular semi-annual audits.



- 164 -
ANNEX 3-21
Page 3 of 3
Part E.   Specialist Services and Fellowships/Local Training
9.        Specialist services and training abroad, including audit
services, valued at US$5.3 million equivalent, would be contracted in
accordance with IDA's guidelines and on the basis of invitation for
proposals from three to six qualified and experienced consultant firms and
agencies and on an exceptional basis, from individual specialists. Local
training represents US$0.87 million equivalent and would be carried out
under principles and procedures satisfactory to the Bank.
Part F. Participation by Foreign Firms
10.       About 59? of the contracts for works and goods would be procured
through LCB according to procedures acceptable to IDA: if foreign firms
wish to participate under these circumstances, they would be allowed to do
so in accordance with local procedures.
Part G.
11.       The figure of 5? would be specified for the purposes of
paragraph h of Appendix 1 to the guidelines (related to any material
modification or waiver of the terms and conditions of contracts or granting
a material extension of the stipulated time, or issuing any change order
under such contract which would increase the cost of contracts by more than
5 of the original price).

ANNEX 3-23
ISLAMIC REPUBLIC OF MAURITANIA
EDUCATION SECTOR RESTRUCTURING PROJECT
Government and Local Contributions
1.         The Government's financial contribution to the project is
estimated at UM 49 million, equivalent to US$0.68 million or 2Z of the
total project cost. The Government contribution represents 20Z of the
operating costs, except those related to the Maritime Training Center,
where the private sector contribution allows the reduction of government
counterpart financing to 16Z.
2.         The contributions provided by local communities and the private
sector, generated from the parents' associations (APEs) and local taxes for
the school construction program, and by the industrial fisheries sector for
supporting a portion of the recurrent costs of the Maritime Training
Center, are estimated at about UM 114 million, equivalent to US$1.57
million or 42 of total project cost. For the school construction program,
the local communities would finance in kind (labor, local building
materials, sanitary facilities and fencing) and through cash contributions,
which should represent 50Z of the construction costs.
3.         The table below shows the breakdown of the Government, local
communities and private sector contributions by expenditure category and
calendar year.
